### Post by Mazza558 on 2009-03-31
**April 2009 Desktop Screenshot Thread**
**April 2009 Desktops - Posting Guidelines**
> 
* Stay within the board rules, no matter how hot you may believe the wallpaper/screen shot to be.
* If you are going to quote, there isn't a need to quote an img-embeded picture - Just don't do it. Please just reference the post by page number/page link/etc.
* Off Topic Posts will be edited or removed.
* The desktops thread is not to be used as a means to post explicit or suggestive, and provocative images (they must be safe for your kids and/or boss to see). Please help to keep the thread relevant and safe to browse for everyone.
* The moderators of this forum reserve the right to edit or remove your posts as necessary so they may comply with our Community Rule set.
* Please use reduced-size thumbnails, where possible, out of respect for people running on lower bandwidth or screen resolutions.
* To avoid having users having to ask you for them. we request that you format your posts in the following order:

Themes: Name/where you got it (with link would be nice).

Wallpaper: Name/where you got it (with link would be nice).

Icons: Name/where you got it (with link would be nice).

Programs: Name/where you got it (with link would be nice).

*Important Note: Any image posted that is over 800 x 600 will be removed! Use a thumbnail or use a text link to your image. If your image is removed, this is why.*

Well, it's April where I am ... so let the madness begin!

Here's my desktop for April. Simple, white, clean and clear.

---

### Post by BobCFC on 2009-04-01
Lost a lot of quality converting to jpegs, all the grainy parts are just screenshot artifacts to get the size down

[[img]http://f.imagehost.org/t/0827/empty.jpg[/img]](http://f.imagehost.org/0827/empty.jpg)

[[img]http://f.imagehost.org/t/0768/home.jpg[/img]](http://f.imagehost.org/0768/home.jpg)

[[img]http://f.imagehost.org/t/0980/minefield.jpg[/img]](http://f.imagehost.org/0980/minefield.jpg)


Wallpaper [http://bobbyperux.deviantart.com/art/Auros-Wallpaper-65980603](http://bobbyperux.deviantart.com/art/Auros-Wallpaper-65980603)

Custom Icons,  
 * uses Erectus as a base: [http://www.gnome-look.org/content/show.php/Erectus?content=100254](http://www.gnome-look.org/content/show.php/Erectus?content=100254) (which in turn is based on Elementary icons)
 * Stop/Refresh icons hacked form the Strata Human firefox theme and modified to be more Tango (give border to roof of home)
 * Many of the 512x512 Mac Icons are taken from the iLeopard Icons Pack SE [http://rs110.rapidshare.com/files/85866864/iLeopard_Icon_Pack_SE.zip](http://rs110.rapidshare.com/files/85866864/iLeopard_Icon_Pack_SE.zip)
 * The blue folder icon from Aquave project (only visible at bottom of first image, but that is my main folder icon) [http://lbaumann.com/aquave/](http://lbaumann.com/aquave/)
 * Most other icons were found on Deviant Art.  I have bookmark some of them on my Favourites Page [http://bobcfc.deviantart.com/favourites/](http://bobcfc.deviantart.com/favourites/)

GTK is hacked version of Human Reprise [http://www.gnome-look.org/content/show.php/Human-Reprise?content=98045](http://www.gnome-look.org/content/show.php/Human-Reprise?content=98045) with custom scrollbars from another them which I can't remember

Emerald is hacked version of Bayou 2 White with the titlebar text set to the right, changed to Myriad Pro Semicondensed (sorry cant' find a link)

Or Metacity theme if not in the mood for emerald is currently Mui Whitebar Mod [http://www.gnome-look.org/content/show.php/Miu+Whitebar+Mod?content=101023](http://www.gnome-look.org/content/show.php/Miu+Whitebar+Mod?content=101023) (The screenshot at G-L doesn't show the grey metacity that is in the download DOH!)


Firefox font is Deja Vu Condensed Size 14 (goto about:config and add condensed to the end of the font name, firefox can't handle subtypes of font properly)

Firefox theme is hacked icons from Strata Human into classic.jar in the chrome folder of Minefield so that I get the icons but keep the gtk tabs etc. [https://addons.mozilla.org/en-US/firefox/addon/8105](https://addons.mozilla.org/en-US/firefox/addon/8105) 

The grey stripes are from the gallery in the new mozilla plugin Personas [http://www.getpersonas.com/](http://www.getpersonas.com/)

---

### Post by eightmillion on 2009-04-01
> **olskar said:**
> Almost all of the really nice screenshots I've seen in this thread (there are nice gnome too) is KDE4. 

It's very nice! But is Kubuntu using the new notifications from Ubuntu?

KDE 4 has its own notification system called extenders. They get themed by the plasma theme. The cool thing is, for things like copy jobs, you can grab one and detach it from the system tray and drop it on your desktop, and it becomes a regular plasmoid like any other widget. They look like this:

[IMG]http://f.imagehost.org/0608/extendergrouping3.png[/IMG]

---

### Post by connorh123 on 2009-04-03

---

### Post by spcwingo on 2009-04-03
> **connorh123 said:**
> I installed wbar, but is there a guide that you followed to get it working?
Either that, or how do I find it once I installed it?

I wrote a startup script to launch it (see below).  Just copy/paste in gedit, then save the file as ~/.wbar.sh and auto lanuch it by going under system>preferences>sessions>add.  Under command browse to the script and you're done.  Just log out and back in and wbar should be there.  Here's the script:

```
#!/bin/sh

(sleep 7s && wbar -bpress -above-desk -pos bottom -isize 50.0 -idist 12.0 -nanim 3.0 -zoomf 1.8 -jumpf 1.0 -balfa 85.0 -falfa 100.0) &
```

Let me know if that gets you fixed up.

I forgot to add that if you want to use custom icons/commands/backgrounds that you need to create a custom .wbar file in your home directory.  Just copy/paste the one under /usr/share/wbar/ to your ~ directory to use as a template.  Just don't forget to rename from dot.wbar to .wbar.

---

### Post by SomeGuyDude on 2009-04-04
> **Vexed Arcanist said:**
> Can I get a copy of your conky config?

```
alignment top_left
border_margin 5
border_width 1
default_color bbbbbb
double_buffer yes
draw_borders no
draw_outline no
draw_shades no
gap_x 5
gap_y -1
maximum_width 760
no_buffers yes
override_utf8_locale yes
own_window_colour eeeeee
own_window_hints undecorated,below,skip_taskbar,skip_pager,sticky
own_window_transparent yes
own_window_type override
own_window yes
stippled_borders 0
update_interval 5
uppercase no
use_spacer yes
use_xft yes
xftfont Nu:size=9
trayer --edge top --align right --widthtype request --heighttype pixel --height 20 --transparent true --alpha 255

TEXT
${color eeeeee}${time %I:%M %p}$color ${time %A, %b %d %Y} ${color} | CPU: ${color eeeeee}$cpu %$color | ${color eeeeee}${voffset 1}${membar 6,80}${offset -80}${voffset -1}${color 000044}Mem${color eeeeee}${offset 60}${color}  | ${voffset 1}${color eeeeee}${fs_bar 6,80 /home}${offset -80}${color 000044}${voffset -1}Home${color eeeeee}${offset 60}${color} | ${voffset 1}${color eeeeee}${fs_bar 6,80 /}${offset -80}${voffset -1}${color 000044}Root${color eeeeee}${offset 60} ${color}| ${color}Battery: ${color eeeeee}${battery}  ${color}| ${color}Temp: ${color eeeeee}${acpitemp}C
Email: ${color eeeeee}${execi 300 python ~/scripts/gmail.py}  ${color}| Arch:${color eeeeee} ${texeci 3600 perl ~/scripts/conky-updates.pl}  ${color}| Weather: ${color eeeeee}${execi 3600 python ~/scripts/conkyForecast.py --location=USPA0796 --datatype=HT -i} ${color}| ${color}$mpd_status ${color eeeeee} ${scroll 75 ${mpd_smart}    }
```

I wanted a way to combined everything into one line. The problem with a lot of conky setups is they're always behind something, so while it looks nice with all of your windows minimized, open up a browser, media player, chat program, and a file manager and everything's gone.

Note: this uses a GMail script, Arch update script, and weather script.

---

### Post by Vexed Arcanist on 2009-04-04
> **SomeGuyDude said:**
> 
I wanted a way to combined everything into one line. The problem with a lot of conky setups is they're always behind something, so while it looks nice with all of your windows minimized, open up a browser, media player, chat program, and a file manager and everything's gone.

Note: this uses a GMail script, Arch update script, and weather script.

Thanks, I mainly wanted to see how you had the drive info written in the displayed 'fill line'.

### Post by etnlIcarus on 2009-04-05
> **s_spiff said:**
> Fabulous setup! 
Can you tell me how do I go about getting that whole RSS part on your desktop?
I'm yet to install xfce though.

$ sudo apt-get install conky

add this to a text file called $HOME/.conkyrc

```
own_window_title conkyrss

max_user_text 20000

use_xft yes
xftfont Segoe Semibold:size=6
override_utf8_locale yes
xftalpha 1

update_interval 1
draw_shades no
default_shade_color 2525ff
draw_outline no
default_outline_color 2525ff
draw_borders no
stippled_borders no
border_margin 0
border_width 1

no_buffers yes
uppercase no
double_buffer yes
use_spacer none

default_color ffffff
color0 ffffff
color1 cfdfdf
color2 bfbfbf
color3 0a0a0a #111111 #1a1a1a #720000
color4 080808 #101010

own_window yes
own_window_colour 080808
own_window_transparent no
own_window_type dock
own_window_hints undecorate,sticky,skip_taskbar,skip_pager,below
background yes
alignment bottom_left
gap_x -2
gap_y 20
minimum_size 1440 0

TEXT
${voffset -3}
${voffset -5}${font LucidaMacBold:size=7}${color}${goto 20}SBS News | World${goto 105}${color ff7e00}${voffset 1}${fs_bar 6,15 /fakelol/}${color}${goto 106}${voffset -2}rss${voffset 1}${goto 220}SBS News | Aust${goto 300}${color ff7e00}${voffset 1}${fs_bar 6,15 /fakelol/}${color}${goto 301}${voffset -2}rss${voffset 1}${goto 420}ABC News | World${goto 509}${color ff7e00}${voffset 1}${fs_bar 6,15 /fakelol/}${color}${goto 510}${voffset -2}rss${voffset 1}${goto 620}ABC News | Aust${goto 704}${color ff7e00}${voffset 1}${fs_bar 6,15 /fakelol/}${color}${goto 705}${voffset -2}rss${voffset 1}${goto 820}BBC News | World${goto 908}${color ff7e00}${voffset 1}${fs_bar 6,15 /fakelol/}${color}${goto 909}${voffset -2}rss${voffset 1}${goto 1020}News Ltd Garbage | SA${goto 1129}${color ff7e00}${voffset 1}${fs_bar 6,15 /fakelol/}${color}${goto 1130}${voffset -2}rss${voffset 1}${goto 1220}Slashdot | Geek${goto 1297}${color ff7e00}${voffset 1}${fs_bar 6,15 /fakelol/}${color}${goto 1298}${voffset -2}rss${voffset 1}${font}${color1}

${voffset -1}${goto 20}${rss http://www.sbs.com.au/news/rss/Section/Top%20Stories 30 item_title 4}${goto 210}${color4}${fs_bar 10,100 /fakelol/}${color1}${goto 220}${rss http://www.sbs.com.au/news/rss/Section/National 30 item_title 4}${goto 410}${color4}${fs_bar 10,100 /fakelol/}${color1}${goto 420}${rss http://www.abc.net.au/news/indexes/world/rss.xml 30 item_title 4}${goto 610}${color4}${fs_bar 10,100 /fakelol/}${color1}${goto 620}${rss http://www.abc.net.au/news/indexes/idx-australia/rss.xml 30 item_title 4}${goto 810}${color4}${fs_bar 10,100 /fakelol/}${color1}${goto 820}${rss http://newsrss.bbc.co.uk/rss/newsonline_world_edition/front_page/rss.xml 30 item_title 4}${goto 1010}${color4}${fs_bar 10,100 /fakelol/}${color1}${goto 1020}${rss http://feeds.news.com.au/public/rss/2.0/anow_state_191.xml 30 item_title 4}${goto 1210}${color4}${fs_bar 10,100 /fakelol/}${color1}${goto 1220}${rss http://rss.slashdot.org/Slashdot/slashdot 30 item_title 4}${goto 1420}${color4}${fs_bar 10,100 /fakelol/}${color1}
```

Create a startup entry for conky.

If you don't have Segoe Semibold and LucidaMacBold, you're going to have to choose different fonts and compensate for their different metrics (the ${fs_bar 10,100 /fakelol/}'s create solid black boxes to prevent text from overlapping but their vertical alignment might be off for different fonts/font sizes).

I really should create a variant on my conkyrc for use with the generic truetype fonts.

Create a startup entry for conky.

If you don't have Segoe Semibold and LucidaMacBold, you're going to have to choose different fonts and compensate for their different metrics (the ${fs_bar 10,100 /fakelol/}'s create solid black boxes to prevent text from overlapping but their vertical alignment might be off for different fonts/font sizes).

I really should create a variant on my conkyrc for use with the generic truetype fonts.

Created a variant which uses the generic Sans font. All you need to do is add the feeds you want to use where it says, "###NEWS FEED 1 URL###", etc. at the bottom of the conkyrc:

```
own_window_title conkyrss

max_user_text 20000

use_xft yes
xftfont Sans:size=6
override_utf8_locale yes
xftalpha 1

update_interval 1
draw_shades no
default_shade_color 2525ff
draw_outline no
default_outline_color 2525ff
draw_borders no
stippled_borders no
border_margin 0
border_width 1

no_buffers yes
uppercase no
double_buffer yes
use_spacer none

default_color ffffff
color0 ffffff
color1 cfdfdf
color2 bfbfbf
color3 0a0a0a
color4 080808

own_window yes
own_window_colour 080808
own_window_transparent no
own_window_type dock
own_window_hints undecorate,sticky,skip_taskbar,skip_pager,below
background yes
alignment bottom_left
gap_x 1
gap_y 20
minimum_size 1440 0

TEXT
${voffset -3}

### Post by eightmillion on 2009-04-05
> **SoftVision said:**
> Are you running KDE 4.3 from svn by any chance? I haven't seen Air for KDE 4.2 anywhere.

I'm running 4.2.2. The Air plasma theme is from the KDE SVN repository. You can get by checking it out of svn and putting it in *~/.kde/share/apps/desktoptheme*. The command to do that is *svn co svn://anonsvn.kde.org/home/kde/trunk/playground/base/plasma/desktoptheme/air/* . Or you can download [this tarball]("http://lyricsdownloader.googlecode.com/files/air_plasma_theme.tar.bz2") and extract it in your desktoptheme directory.

### Post by gjoellee on 2009-04-05
This is my KDEmod desktop. It is KDE 4.2.2.

Theme: Elegance
Distro: Arch Linux
Resolution: 1280x1024
Wallpaper Resolution: 1280x1204

Some information about Stask:
It is available from the AUR: [http://aur.archlinux.org/packages.php?ID=24090](http://aur.archlinux.org/packages.php?ID=24090) or at kde-look: [http://www.kde-look.org/content/show.php/STasks?content=99739](http://www.kde-look.org/content/show.php/STasks?content=99739)

NOTE: The Lime Wire notification icons looks really bad, ind if you wonder why I don't use Frostwire is because it is not in verison 5 which is a lot better. When frostwire comes to v.5 I am moving to Frostwire.


I am running the "Stask" plasmoid. Stask makes the window management in KDE similar to how it is in Windows 7. It is awesome!

### Post by Vexed Arcanist on 2009-04-05

### Post by Mazza558 on 2009-04-06
Trying out Gnome Shell, just built it from source.

I'm beginning to like it, I have to say. It puts a lot more emphasis on organising your apps. You can drag them to and from the different workspaces in the same fashion as one of the compiz plugins.

With my FOSS ATI driver, the compositing is very slow but usable enough to... well... use it. My fonts have gone a bit blurry too. Well, considering it's pre-alpha, not bad at all. If it gets faster then it'll be a very usable system.

Oh, and the font is DecoTech TL...can't figure out how to attach a .tff file.

That font is available at dafont.com

This one is much crisper and cleaner.  
Get it here: [http://linux.softpedia.com/get/Desktop-Environment/Themes/iRoll-1-4-42211.shtml](http://linux.softpedia.com/get/Desktop-Environment/Themes/iRoll-1-4-42211.shtml)

Oh, and to anybody who might say "well, if you want linux to look like a Mac, then why don't you get a mac", etc...because I *love* Linux!!!
I personally have no desire or need for a mac as linux is my os of choice for good reason.  

And the beautiful aqua theme does not "desecrate thy sacred Linux". :p

### Post by Chemical Imbalance on 2009-04-09
> **jyaan said:**
> [[IMG]http://img254.imageshack.us/img254/2881/linuxzu5.th.png[/IMG]](http://img254.imageshack.us/my.php?image=linuxzu5.png)
To this very day, I miss this theme I had w/ Baghira on KDE3. If I could achieve what I had with KDE4, I would definitely switch back over to KDE. Unfortunately KDE4 went in a totally different direction, and both the global menu and Baghira have no replacements. :(

Maybe give this one a try then:

[http://linux.softpedia.com/get/Desktop-Environment/Themes/iRoll-1-4-42211.shtml](http://linux.softpedia.com/get/Desktop-Environment/Themes/iRoll-1-4-42211.shtml)

its what i'm using, and its the best gtk mac theme ive seen yet

make sure after you install it that you hit customize and manually choose the window decoration bc I believe it doesn't show initially after you install.

yes, it´s awn at the bottom, with full transaprent background, and i use the sidebar screenlet for a full-width background instead

[attach]109316[/attach]

screen running dvtm, which in turn is running MyMan, tty-clock, alpine and vimwiki. MOC, htop and mc are also up, on different screen windows. Memory profile is under 28Mb, CPU usage is under 20 percent of 550MHz. Everything is running against the framebuffer, no X, and the console font is Terminus.

All brought to you courtesy of Crux Linux. ;)

### Post by Giant Speck on 2009-04-10
> **eightmillion said:**
> For the past couple of weeks I've been kind of mapping out in my head a plasmoid to do what knewsticker did, with the intent of writing such a thing. Are there any special features that I should be aware of? I only ran it once or twice.


This is all I remember about Knewsticker:

- Ability to add, edit, and remove RSS feeds.
- Ability to change text color, background color, and text hover color.
- Ability to change text font and size.
- Ability to change text speed (and possibly scroll direction).
- Clicking on a news story opened the story in the user's default browser.

It would probably not be difficult to make a Plasmoid for this.  I really wish someone would come up with a Gnome panel applet that does it, since you can't run Plasmoids in Gnome.

> **chucky chuckaluck said:**
> well, i've got an emerald windec. that is opaque and i was wondering if i could make it a little see-through.

It depends on the theme engine used to make the theme.  If it is a pixmap theme, then you'd have to use GIMP to make the images transparent.  If it is a vrunner theme, then you can use the opacity option to get the desired amount of transparency.

---

### Post by chucky chuckaluck on 2009-04-10
> **Giant Speck said:**
> If it is a vrunner theme, then you can use the opacity option to get the desired amount of transparency.

where is that option? (i must be staring straight at it.)

---

### Post by Giant Speck on 2009-04-10
> **chucky chuckaluck said:**
> where is that option? (i must be staring straight at it.)

Open up the Emerald Themer program, and click on the "Edit Theme" tab.

Click on the drop down list and select vrunner, for example.  You have to select it from the drop down list even if it is the one showing, or else you won't see the engine-specific options.

---

### Post by chucky chuckaluck on 2009-04-10
> **Giant Speck said:**
> Open up the Emerald Themer program, and click on the "Edit Theme" tab.

Click on the drop down list and select vrunner, for example.  You have to select it from the drop down list even if it is the one showing, or else you won't see the engine-specific options.

ah, that was it! thanks, dude. you're a giant among specks.

### Post by Sealbhach on 2009-04-11
> **Ticketoride said:**
> I see People using Themes.

I don´t have any Menu Item of Themes installed, nor are any Items available in ¨Add & Remove¨. I found some gtk-something & gnome Apps in Synapsis and installed them, but H*ll if I know where they went off to after the Install. I still have no Menu Item I can click on dealing with Themes.



Yes, it's a little confusing at first. When you download a theme, say from the Gnome-Look website, it's usually a tar.gz file. Once you have downloaded this to the desktop, right-click on desktop, select Change desktop background, then click on the themes tab. Then drag and drop your tar.gz file into there. Most of them work that way, although some don't.

That GTK change theme thing you downloaded? That's in your menu in Applications/System Tools. It's useful as it smooths over the theme changes, especially helps in changing the panels.


.

### Post by etnlIcarus on 2009-04-12

Wall is called, "water in the leaf". Not sure where I found it (might be from art.gnome.org or interfacelift.com). I'm also on speed limiting ATM so I'd rather not have to upload it.

```
own_window_title conkystats

use_xft yes
xftfont LucidaMacBold:size=7
override_utf8_locale yes
xftalpha 1

update_interval 1
draw_shades no
default_shade_color ff0000
draw_outline no
default_outline_color 151515
draw_borders no
stippled_borders no
border_margin 0
border_width 1

no_buffers yes
uppercase no
double_buffer yes
use_spacer none

default_color 303030
color1 252525
color2 080808
color3 ffffff

own_window yes
own_window_colour 280808 #121212
own_window_transparent yes
own_window_type dock
own_window_hints undecorate,sticky,skip_taskbar,skip_pager,below
background yes
alignment bottom_middle
gap_x 0
gap_y -27
minimum_size 960 0

${voffset 0}${goto 10}${color}72gb: ${voffset 1}${color3}${fs_bar 6,18 /} ${voffset -1}${color}${fs_used_perc /}% ${goto 90}75gb: ${voffset 1}${color3}${fs_bar 6,18 /media/windows_drive} ${voffset -1}${color}${fs_used_perc /media/windows_drive}%${goto 170}10gb: ${voffset 1}${color3}${fs_bar 6,18 /media/shared_drive} ${voffset -1}${color}${fs_used_perc /media/shared_drive}%${goto 245}|${goto 260}d: ${downspeed eth0}Kb/s${goto 310}${color2}(${totaldown eth0})${color}${goto 380}u: ${upspeed eth0}Kb/s ${goto 430}${color2}(${totalup eth0})${goto 495}${color FFAB7A}Internode  ${color}used:${goto 575}${execi 30 iheart8mil.sh}%${goto 605}${color2}(${execi 30 iheart8mil2.sh}MiB)${goto 665}${color}|${goto 675}cpu: ${voffset 1}${color3}${cpugraph 6,18} ${voffset -1}${color}${cpu}%${goto 750}ram: ${voffset 1}${color3}${membar 6,18} ${voffset -1}${color}${memperc}%${goto 825}swap: ${voffset 1}${color3}${swapbar 6,18} ${voffset -1}${color}${swapperc}%

TEXT
${voffset -3}${color2}${goto 0}${fs_bar 15,80 /fakelol/}${goto 100}${fs_bar 15,80 /fakelol/}${goto 200}${fs_bar 15,80 /fakelol/}${goto 340}${fs_bar 15,80 /fakelol/}${goto 440}${fs_bar 15,80 /fakelol/}${goto 540}${fs_bar 15,80 /fakelol/}${goto 680}${fs_bar 15,80 /fakelol/}${goto 780}${fs_bar 15,80 /fakelol/}${goto 880}${fs_bar 15,80 /fakelol/}
${voffset -25}${color1}${goto 0}${fs_bar 15,80 /}${goto 100}${fs_bar 15,80 /media/windows_drive}${goto 200}${fs_bar 15,80 /media/shared_drive}${goto 340}${downspeedgraph eth0 15,80}${goto 440}${upspeedgraph eth0 15,80}${goto 540}${fs_bar 15,80 /fakelol/}${goto 680}${cpugraph 15,80}${goto 780}${membar 15,80}${goto 880}${swapbar 15,80}
${voffset -19}${color3}${goto 15}72GiB: ${fs_used_perc /}%${goto 115}75GiB: ${fs_used_perc /media/windows_drive}%${goto 215}10GiB: ${fs_used_perc /media/shared_drive}%${goto 350}down: ${downspeed eth0}kB/s${goto 460}up: ${upspeed eth0}kB/s${goto 555}data: ${execi 30 iheart8mil.sh}%${goto 700}CPU: ${cpu}%${goto 800}RAM: ${memperc}%${goto 900}swap: ${swapperc}%

### Post by mjheagle8 on 2009-04-13
if anyone's interested, i just wrote a script that uses dbus to display amarok 2 info in conky. tell me what you think! :)
```

#!/bin/bash
#fetch conky amarok2 information
#by Mjheagle8
#requires: amarok >= 2.0, qdbus

case "$1" in
version)
echo `qdbus org.kde.amarok / org.freedesktop.MediaPlayer.Identity`
;;
artist)
char=`qdbus org.kde.amarok /Player org.freedesktop.MediaPlayer.GetMetadata | grep artist: | wc -m`
artist=`qdbus org.kde.amarok /Player org.freedesktop.MediaPlayer.GetMetadata | grep artist: | cut -c 9-$char`
echo $artist
;;
title)
char=`qdbus org.kde.amarok /Player org.freedesktop.MediaPlayer.GetMetadata | grep title: | wc -m`
title=`qdbus org.kde.amarok /Player org.freedesktop.MediaPlayer.GetMetadata | grep title: | cut -c 8-$char`
echo $title
;;
album)
char=`qdbus org.kde.amarok /Player org.freedesktop.MediaPlayer.GetMetadata | grep album: | wc -m`
album=`qdbus org.kde.amarok /Player org.freedesktop.MediaPlayer.GetMetadata | grep album: | cut -c 8-$char`
echo $album
;;
year)
char=`qdbus org.kde.amarok /Player org.freedesktop.MediaPlayer.GetMetadata | grep year: | wc -m`
year=`qdbus org.kde.amarok /Player org.freedesktop.MediaPlayer.GetMetadata | grep year: | cut -c 7-$char`
echo $year
;;
genre)
char=`qdbus org.kde.amarok /Player org.freedesktop.MediaPlayer.GetMetadata | grep genre: | wc -m`
genre=`qdbus org.kde.amarok /Player org.freedesktop.MediaPlayer.GetMetadata | grep genre: | cut -c 8-$char`
echo $genre
;;
bitrate)
char=`qdbus org.kde.amarok /Player org.freedesktop.MediaPlayer.GetMetadata | grep audio-bitrate: | wc -m`
bitrate=`qdbus org.kde.amarok /Player org.freedesktop.MediaPlayer.GetMetadata | grep audio-bitrate: | cut -c 16-$char`
echo $bitrate' Kb/s'
;;
rating)
char=`qdbus org.kde.amarok /Player org.freedesktop.MediaPlayer.GetMetadata | grep rating: | wc -m`
rating=`qdbus org.kde.amarok /Player org.freedesktop.MediaPlayer.GetMetadata | grep rating: | cut -c 9-$char`
echo $rating
;;
type)
char=`qdbus org.kde.amarok /Player org.freedesktop.MediaPlayer.GetMetadata | grep location: | wc -m`
chari=`expr $char - 3`
type=`qdbus org.kde.amarok /Player org.freedesktop.MediaPlayer.GetMetadata | grep location: | cut -c $chari-$char`
echo $type
;;
time)
pos=`qdbus org.kde.amarok /Player org.freedesktop.MediaPlayer.PositionGet`
pos=`expr $pos / 1000`
char=`qdbus org.kde.amarok /Player org.freedesktop.MediaPlayer.GetMetadata | grep mtime: | wc -m`
time=`qdbus org.kde.amarok /Player org.freedesktop.MediaPlayer.GetMetadata | grep mtime: | cut -c 8-$char`
time=`expr $time / 1000`
echo $pos' / '$time
;;
timeperc)
pos=`qdbus org.kde.amarok /Player org.freedesktop.MediaPlayer.PositionGet`
pos=`expr $pos / 10`
char=`qdbus org.kde.amarok /Player org.freedesktop.MediaPlayer.GetMetadata | grep mtime: | wc -m`
time=`qdbus org.kde.amarok /Player org.freedesktop.MediaPlayer.GetMetadata | grep mtime: | cut -c 8-$char`
time=`expr $time / 1000`
perc=`expr $pos / $time`
echo $perc
;;
esac

```

### Post by Daisuke_Aramaki on 2009-04-13
@eightmillion

Fantastic as always.

@purposeofreason

The terminal font is good old terminus. And the dwm workspace font is cure. 
As far as Lunar goes, yes it is a source based distro that was forked out of sorcerer operating system. I had been a longtime gentoo user some years back, but i had problems after problems with it, that i was done with source based distro and went to binary distros like debian, ubuntu and arch. but a year ago or so, wanted to go back to using the source, and heard about lunar and haven't turned back eversince. its fantastic, and the package management is pretty good, and it is very easy for me to write my own modules and use up to date source code all the time. Even the moonbase (lunar's repository) is updated almost once every week, with new packages when the program author/s release a new tarball. And also since lunar just provides just a bootstrap system, i can have complete control over the way programs are built on my machine.

---

### Post by eightmillion on 2009-04-13
> **OutOfReach said:**
> Ahhh. So. Beautiful.
Mind sharing details?

Thanks. Here are the details. The plasma theme is Eleonora with the system tray replaced with the one from Oxygen. The wallpaper came from [this pack]("http://mareklevak.deviantart.com/art/Spring-wallpapers-118969674"). The icons are Oxygen Refit 2 Black with different folder icons. I've attached the bespin config and color scheme and folder icon. To switch the icon, I just run this command:
[PHP]for i in 128 64 48 32 24 16;do convert -geometry ${i}x${i} -sharpen 0x.4 folder2.png ~/.kde/share/icons/OxygenRefit2-black-version/${i}x${i}/places/folder.png;done[/PHP]

Edit: Thanks Daisuke_Aramaki.

### Post by gjoellee on 2009-04-14
> **dbbolton said:**
> ROFLMFAO


Question for KDE users- what do you recommend to do with GTK apps?

Usually I just choose some generic style with my .gtkrc.mine , but I was wondering if there is some way to make GTK apps mimic the current QT style (chiefly the fonts).

I installed "lxappearance" which allows you to theme GTK applications in KDE without configuring the .gtkrc files. Then I downloaded a GTK theme that was inspired by KDE's theme and extracted the downloaded theme to /usr/share/themes. 

Then I opened lxappearance by typing "lxappearance" in the terminal and changed the theme and icon theme to the KDE lookalike themes. But the when I open any applications that require a password they still look bad. 

The fix is: Open lxapeearance with sudo. In the temrinal type "sudo lxappearance" change the themes to the KDE lookalike and now root applications look good to. :p

### Post by eightmillion on 2009-04-14
> **dbbolton said:**
> ROFLMFAO


Question for KDE users- what do you recommend to do with GTK apps?

Usually I just choose some generic style with my .gtkrc.mine , but I was wondering if there is some way to make GTK apps mimic the current QT style (chiefly the fonts).
There is something called GTK-Qt engine that allows GTK apps to use your Qt style and fonts. In Ubuntu the package is called gtk-qt-engine. I think it's install by default. If it's installed, there should be a page under appearance in system settings where you can check "Use my KDE style in GTK applications" and "Use my KDE fonts in GTK applications".
> **JECHO said:**
> I just installed Kubuntu after seeing your screenshots lol

... Im currently trying to install bespin and when i run the configure script it is asking me to input a "Path to Qt4"... do you know what to enter?
If you're running Ubuntu, you can install it from the repos. The package is kde4-style-bespin. Otherwise, the way to build most KDE software is to ignore any configure scripts and use cmake. Run these commands from your bespin source directory:
```

mkdir build
cd build
cmake .. -DCMAKE_INSTALL_PREFIX=`kde-config --prefix`
make
sudo make install
```
If you want to try to use the configure script, then qt4 includes are usually in /usr/include/qt4 if the qt4 dev packages are installed.

---

### Post by JECHO on 2009-04-14
> **eightmillion said:**
> There is something called GTK-Qt engine that allows GTK apps to use your Qt style and fonts. In Ubuntu the package is called gtk-qt-engine. I think it's install by default. If it's installed, there should be a page under appearance in system settings where you can check "Use my KDE style in GTK applications" and "Use my KDE fonts in GTK applications".

If you're running Ubuntu, you can install it from the repos. The package is kde4-style-bespin. Otherwise, the way to build most KDE software is to ignore any configure scripts and use cmake. Run these commands from your bespin source directory:
```

mkdir build
cd build
cmake .. -DCMAKE_INSTALL_PREFIX=`kde-config --prefix`
make
sudo make install
```
If you want to try to use the configure script, then qt4 includes are usually in /usr/include/qt4 if the qt4 dev packages are installed.

thanks man, the package from the repos worked great :) 


one last question... how do i use the folder icon you provided? I see you say to run that command but does the folder have to go into a certain directory or somehting?

### Post by eightmillion on 2009-04-14
> **JECHO said:**
> thanks man, the package from the repos worked great :) 


one last question... how do i use the folder icon you provided? I see you say to run that command but does the folder have to go into a certain directory or somehting?

No problem. The folder icon just has to be in your current working directory when you run that bit of script, or you can change folder2.png in that line to point to an absolute path like ~/folder2.png . I suppose I should also mention that imagemagick must be installed too.

### Post by eightmillion on 2009-04-15
> **RiceMonster said:**
> 
Also, your desktop looks great. I see you're using Konqueror. Can you get and adblock equivalent on that? (I know epiphany has one)

To answer this question, yes, Konqueror has adblock built in. You just have to download a filter list and import it. Also, Firefox adblock lists are compatible with Konqueror.

### Post by 5BallJuggler on 2009-04-15
> **Sealbhach said:**
> That's cool. Want to share the Conky goodness? (conkyrc)


.

Thanks very much,
These are the latest conky files

.conkyslowstart #this file calls all the scripts
```
#! /bin/bash

if pidof conky | grep [0-9] > /dev/null
then
 exec killall conky
else
sleep 3 &&
conky -d -c /home/phil/.conkyrc &
sleep 35 &&
conky -d -c /home/phil/.conkylc &
sleep 4 &&
conky -d -c /home/phil/.conkymid &
sleep 5 &&
conky -d -c /home/phil/.conkymus &
sleep 1 &&
conky -d -c /home/phil/.conkyrt &
sleep 2 &&
conky -d -c /home/phil/.conkyrb &
exit
fi
```

.conkymid #this is only fortune cookie
```
alignment top_left
background no
border_width 1
cpu_avg_samples 2
default_color 94959C
default_outline_color 94959C
default_shade_color 94959C
double_buffer yes
draw_borders no
draw_graph_borders no
draw_outline no
draw_shades no
gap_x 273
gap_y 10 
maximum_width 478
max_port_monitor_connections 64
max_specials 2048
max_user_text 32768
minimum_size 478 580
net_avg_samples 2
no_buffers yes
out_to_console no
own_window_colour black
own_window_hints undecorated,below,sticky,skip_taskbar,skip_pager
own_window_transparent yes
own_window_type normal
own_window yes
stippled_borders 2
text_buffer_size 1024
update_interval 1
uppercase no
use_spacer none
use_xft yes
xftalpha 0.8
xftfont  Purisa:size=7

TEXT
${offset 180}${color #016BFF}${font Purisa:size=12}Fortune Cookie
${voffset -3}${font Purisa:size=9}${execi 150 fortune | fold -s -w70} 
```

.conkyrt #this is the time and date
```
alignment top_right
background no
border_width 2
cpu_avg_samples 2
default_color 94959C
default_outline_color 94959C
default_shade_color 94959C
double_buffer yes

${voffset -5}${execpi 2 cat /sys/class/net/wlan0/wireless/link | xargs ~/wireless.sh}${wireless_link_bar 12,242 wlan0}

${voffset -5}${upspeedgraph wlan0 24,248 016BFF ff0000}

colorize.sh #this is gives differing colours depending on battery level
```
#!/bin/bash
# colorize.sh

DYING=15
FINE=40
CONNECT=`acpi -b | cut -c17`

if [[ D = $CONNECT ]]
then
  if [[ $1 < $DYING ]] 
  then
  echo "\${color ff0000}"	# DYING
  elif [[ $1 > $FINE ]]
  then
  echo "\${color 00ff00}"	# FULL
  else 
  echo "\${color ffff00}"	# FINE
  fi
else
  echo "\${color 00ff00}"	# CHARGING
  fi

exit 0
```

wireless.sh #this is gives differing colours depending on wireless strength
```
#!/bin/bash
# wireless.sh

DYING=30
FINE=55

if [[ $1 < $DYING ]] 
then
echo "\${color ff0000}"	# DYING
elif [[ $1 > $FINE ]]
then
echo "\${color 00ff00}"	# FULL
else 
echo "\${color ffff00}"	# FINE
fi


exit 0
```

The colors from my previous post are from my old Xdefaults. So you can simply use the colors here.

```

xterm*background:        #222222
xterm*foreground:        #ddccbb

!black
*color0:  #222222
*color8:  #554444

!red
*color1:  #884422
*color9:  #cc5533

!green
*color2:  #778800
*color10: #88aa22

!yellow
*color3:  #887733
*color11: #aa9955

!blue
*color4:  #8866cc
*color12: #9977dd

!magneta
*color5:  #885500
*color13: #996600

!cyan
*color6:  #5555aa
*color14: #7777aa

!white
*color7:  #bbaa99
*color15: #ddccaa

```

### Post by sertse on 2009-04-16
This is why I run evilwm. :D :D

evilwm (is there as floating wm lighter? tinywm has focus issues when I tried)
gmrun

Keyboard shortcuts created directly using xbitmap (less bloat! lol). Text login. Lxappearance method of theming through creating a gtkrc also meant is lighter than using xfce-setting-show, and it's daemons. 

Wallpaper... I linked to it in my previous post, but it doesn't matter here - You won't be seeing it at all in evilwm. 

Evilwm is surprisingly usable. Very plain, but I find it was actually less "distracting", after all you meant to be focusing what's inside the window no?

My gripe is that you can't minimise/hide a window though, (only switch between what's in focus) so you'll won't see your wallpaper much...

---

### Post by Vexed Arcanist on 2009-04-16
> **Stan_1936 said:**
> Could you post your conky(clock) rc file?  It looks great.

Sure thing, this conky is all white on the clock (what I am currently using).  Adjusting is done with the colorX colors above the TEXT.  Apple Garamond font available at dafont.com.

```
own_window_title timedate

max_user_text 20000

use_xft yes
xftfont snap:size=9
override_utf8_locale yes
xftalpha 1

update_interval 1
draw_shades no
default_shade_color ffffff
draw_outline no
default_outline_color 252525
draw_borders no
stippled_borders no
border_margin 0
border_width 1

no_buffers yes
uppercase no
double_buffer yes
use_spacer none

default_color 303030
color1 47951C
color2 4476A5
color3 FBFBFB

own_window yes
own_window_colour black
own_window_transparent yes
own_window_type normal
own_window_hints undecorate,sticky,skip_taskbar,skip_pager,below
background yes
alignment top_right
gap_x 0
gap_y 0
minimum_size 150 0

TEXT



${color3}${font Apple Garamond:size=96}${time %H}${voffset -46}${font Apple Garamond:bold:size=38}${time :%M}${voffset -18}${font Apple Garamond:bold:size=18}${time %S}       

${color3}${voffset -16}${alignr}${font Apple Garamond:size=18}${time %A,}    
${voffset -8}${alignr}${time %d %B %Y}  
```

### Post by Giant Speck on 2009-04-17
> **Roanoke said:**
> How did you get that backdrop to conky?

I'm not really good at conky, and mine is a very heavily modified version of the Mira conky.  However, I think it's these two parts of my conky that is creating that background:

```
# Create own window instead of using desktop (required in nautilus)
own_window  yes
own_window_transparent no
own_window_type normal
own_window_title colorconky
own_window_hints undecorate,sticky,skip_taskbar,skip_pager
```

and

```
# Default colors and also border colors
default_color 292929
#default_shade_color white
#default_outline_color black
own_window_colour 171717
```

The colorconky you see indicates that I'm using devilspie to make it translucent.

### Post by Vexed Arcanist on 2009-04-17
> **mrdiego said:**
> Wow your FF is crazy good. One stuff may be Tiny-Menu. But what's Theme you are using by hell ...? :D

Want check it out. You can show me where you got it? Thx

It's Tiny Menu addon (you got that right).

Chromifox Basic (firefox theme)

Then you move everything to the top bar and disable the navigation and bookmarks bars via customize.  Remove any functions you don't really need, like the search box, Home icon, etc.  Any bookmarks you have you simply edit them to remove the text label.  Viola!  You now have a chucky chuckaluck FF original.

---

Honestly, I don't know why most linux distros don't do this by default. Gnome doesn't have Xfce's root warning so it would seem sensible to give users some hint when they're running in, "Windows mode".

<.< Cheap shot, I know.

---

### Post by Daisuke_Aramaki on 2009-04-18
> **sertse said:**
> Yes! Another person who'll try out evilwm! If you're going down that route, also try sithwm, it's evilwm with some extras..

Yours is realllly nice. I don't know where to begin. 

Umm, icons, conky and .bashrc? And is it vcstime you have showing a clock (?) at the corner of your terminals?

Go back in this thread and March screenshots thread, you will find a lot of evilwm screens of mine. i have been alternating between evilwm and dwm for a long time now. i did try sithwm, but i prefer evilwm.

Icons are sun festa, you can find them over at gnome-look.org. The colors come from my Xdefaults. And its zsh, and not bash. Time is piped via my .zshrc, and no vcstime is involved. You can find all my configs, Xdefaults, zshrc, vimrc etc., over at my [dotfiles page]("http://dotfiles.org/~section9/")

Conky is ripped off of a post from freebsd forums. I will upload the same over at my dotfiles page.

But please note, my zshrc is optimized for freebsd. but it should work without issues on linux as well.

Hope that answers your questions.

### Post by mrdiego on 2009-04-18
> **Vexed Arcanist said:**
> It's Tiny Menu addon (you got that right).

Chromifox Basic (firefox theme)

Then you move everything to the top bar and disable the navigation and bookmarks bars via customize.  Remove any functions you don't really need, like the search box, Home icon, etc.  Any bookmarks you have you simply edit them to remove the text label.  Viola!  You now have a chucky chuckaluck FF original.

Thank you very much. I will check it out after I had installed KDE again. I liked the new Jaunty/Gnome very much, too. But in KDE I felt more performance thanks QT 4.5. :) And yes, KDE and Gnome like System-Window-Managers, also both, are great. Hey XCFE surely is a great stuff, too. Unfortunately not what I am looking for ... Everybody with his own taste ... :D

### Post by RiceMonster on 2009-04-20
> **etnlIcarus said:**
> My least favourite is *the new f****ng session manager* which has been driving me up the wall for the last several days. Xfce: now officially as infuriating as Gnome.

What's annoying about it? I haven't payed attention to it, or used it, really.

---

### Post by etnlIcarus on 2009-04-20
> **RiceMonster said:**
> What's annoying about it? I haven't payed attention to it, or used it, really.

It's screwing with conky and xpad. Conky was loading 5 times as many instances as it should have been and xpad kept creating a new blank pad everytime I logged in. 

Plus the session manager has the same idiotic behaviour Gnome had some years ago: open session manager to "save session"; the next time you try to log into your static session the session dialogue will open automatically.

The manager should *only* handle application monitoring and restarting and leave the handling of auto-starting apps to .desktop launchers in the .config/autostart/ directory.

---

### Post by perfectska04 on 2009-04-21
> **SomeGuyDude said:**
> QT can, however, adopt your GTK theme. VERY cool, must be a new feature. Evidence: VLC and Picard (QT) along with Sonata and PCManFM (GTK).

It was available before as a package called "qgtkstyle", but in Jaunty, it's included by default! VLC, Picard, Virtualbox and possibly others all look great in GNOME now.

### Post by Truedream on 2009-04-22
try this:

make a new font.conf in your home folder, log out and log back in. should make fonts look better

```
<?xml version="1.0"?>
<!DOCTYPE fontconfig SYSTEM "fonts.dtd">
<fontconfig>
  <match target="font">
    <edit name="autohint" mode="assign">
      <bool>true</bool>
    </edit>
  </match>
</fontconfig>
```

### Post by eightmillion on 2009-04-22
> **etnlIcarus said:**
> Like your Qt theme. Reminds me of the default E17 look.
Thanks. I can see how you could say that.
> **rkakkar said:**
> how do i get my taskbar in kde to look like that? with the colourful menu logo and the system tray style and everything?
To get your taskbar to look like that, you have to use the Eleonora plasma style. The system tray is from Oxygen. As far as I know, desktop theme details doesn't provide a way of changing just the system tray so I copied the system tray from the Oxygen style. You can do that with a command like this: cp /usr/share/kde4/apps/desktoptheme/default/widgets/systemtray.svgz ~/.kde/share/apps/desktoptheme/Eleonora/widgets/

To get the menu logo, you have to install [lzfy's iKon icon theme]("http://dl.getdropbox.com/u/803597/iKon_2.tar.gz") or [Oxygen Refit Black.]("http://www.kde-look.org/content/show.php/Oxygen+Refit+Black?content=89298")

---

### Post by Daisuke_Aramaki on 2009-04-22
> **Vexed Arcanist said:**
> If I am not mistaken he is using dzen2 with conky-cli...if only I was any good at compiling I would do the same.  If anyone has a Ubuntu package for amd64 conky-cli, I would be very appreciative with a link.

Why would it be difficult to compile conky-cli? you just need to pass the no X option in configure command. 

```
./configure --disable-x11
```

Likewise you can even disable xft fonts, enable mpd, etc.

### Post by SomeGuyDude on 2009-04-22
> **Vexed Arcanist said:**
> If I am not mistaken he is using dzen2 with conky-cli...if only I was any good at compiling I would do the same.  If anyone has a Ubuntu package for amd64 conky-cli, I would be very appreciative with a link.

Actually it's just plain ol' conky. :guitar:

```
alignment top_left
border_margin 5
border_width 1
default_color bbbbbb
double_buffer yes
draw_borders no
draw_outline no
draw_shades no
gap_x 0
gap_y 0
maximum_width 765
no_buffers yes
override_utf8_locale yes
own_window_colour eeeeee
own_window_hints undecorated,below,skip_taskbar,skip_pager,sticky
own_window_transparent yes
own_window_type override
own_window yes
stippled_borders 0
update_interval 5
uppercase no
#use_spacer yes
use_xft yes
xftfont Nu:size=9

TEXT
${offset 19}${color eeeeee}${time %I:%M %p}$color ${time %A, %b %d %Y} ${color} | CPU: ${color eeeeee}$cpu %$color | ${color eeeeee}${voffset 1}${membar 6,75}${offset -75}${voffset -1}${color 000044}Mem${color eeeeee}${offset 55}${color}  | ${voffset 1}${color eeeeee}${fs_bar 6,75 /home}${offset -75}${color 000044}${voffset -1}Home${color eeeeee}${offset 55}${color} | ${voffset 1}${color eeeeee}${fs_bar 6,75 /}${offset -75}${voffset -1}${color 000044}Root${color eeeeee}${offset 55} ${color}| ${color}Battery: ${color eeeeee}${battery}  ${color}| ${color}Temp: ${color eeeeee}${acpitemp}
${voffset -8}${font OpenLogos:size=15}A${font}${voffset -3}${offset 1}Email: ${color eeeeee}${execi 300 python ~/scripts/gmail.py}  ${color}| Arch:${color eeeeee} ${texeci 3550 perl ~/scripts/conky-updates.pl}  ${color}| Weather: ${color eeeeee}${execi 3550 python ~/scripts/conkyForecast.py --location=USPA0796 --datatype=HT -i} ${color}| ${color}$mpd_status ${color eeeeee} ${scroll 75 ${mpd_smart}    }

```

### Post by rkakkar on 2009-04-23
> **eightmillion said:**
> Thanks. I can see how you could say that.

To get your taskbar to look like that, you have to use the Eleonora plasma style. The system tray is from Oxygen. As far as I know, desktop theme details doesn't provide a way of changing just the system tray so I copied the system tray from the Oxygen style. You can do that with a command like this: cp /usr/share/kde4/apps/desktoptheme/default/widgets/systemtray.svgz ~/.kde/share/apps/desktoptheme/Eleonora/widgets/

To get the menu logo, you have to install [lzfy's iKon icon theme]("http://dl.getdropbox.com/u/803597/iKon_2.tar.gz") or [Oxygen Refit Black.]("http://www.kde-look.org/content/show.php/Oxygen+Refit+Black?content=89298")

Thanks! One more question. How can I remove the playlist in Amarok so that only the controls are visible? Like a 'compact amarok window'?

---

Compiz + edge resistance + resize info + some basic math.

### Post by etnlIcarus on 2009-04-23
Conkydings RSS font: [http://ubuntuforums.org/showthread.php?p=7119528#post7119528](http://ubuntuforums.org/showthread.php?p=7119528#post7119528)

Conkyrss config: [http://ubuntuforums.org/showthread.php?p=7126178#post7126178](http://ubuntuforums.org/showthread.php?p=7126178#post7126178)

Version of Conkyrss using generic fonts (ie you don't need to change every voffset and goto value to compensate for different font metrics):

```
own_window_title conkyrss

max_user_text 20000

use_xft yes
xftfont Sans:size=6
override_utf8_locale yes
xftalpha 1

update_interval 1
draw_shades no
default_shade_color 2525ff
draw_outline no
default_outline_color 2525ff
draw_borders no
stippled_borders no
border_margin 0
border_width 1

no_buffers yes
uppercase no
double_buffer yes
use_spacer none

default_color ffffff
color0 ffffff
color1 cfdfdf
color2 bfbfbf
color3 0a0a0a
color4 080808

own_window yes
own_window_colour 080808
own_window_transparent no
own_window_type dock
own_window_hints undecorate,sticky,skip_taskbar,skip_pager,below
background yes
alignment bottom_left
gap_x 1
gap_y 20
minimum_size 1440 0

TEXT

### Post by Daisuke_Aramaki on 2009-04-23
> **Vexed Arcanist said:**
> Indeed, getting it to work with dzen2 seems to have a learning curve I didn't expect, working on that now.

Great. yeah piping the output to dzen2 takes a little bit time for a beginner. But i am sure you will easily figure that out. If you look into some xmonad.hs or other tiling wm configs in dotfiles or github, you will see a lot of instances, where the authors use conky to pipe the stats to dzen2. so its also worthwhile to have a look at such configs as well. good luck anyway.

### Post by eightmillion on 2009-04-24
> **lzfy said:**
> Thanks :)



You have to replace the file mimetypes/inode-directory.png in the .kde/share/icons/%icontheme% folder.

I believe that eightmillion had a script for this.

I've got a one liner that should work.

```
for i in 128 48 64 32 24 16;do convert -geometry ${i}x${i} -sharpen 0x.4 /path/to/icon.png ~/.kde/share/icons/NAMEOFICONTHEME/${i}x${i}/mimetypes/inode-directory.png;done
```

You might have to change the numbers to correspond to the sizes that the icon theme contains. You'll also have to change the path to the icon and icon theme. You might also have to replace folder.png in places like this:
```
for i in 128 48 64 32 24 16;do convert -geometry ${i}x${i} -sharpen 0x.4 /path/to/icon.png ~/.kde/share/icons/NAMEOFICONTHEME/${i}x${i}/places/folder.png;done
```

And if you put additional folder icons in the places folder, then you'll be able to select them as custom icons for folder.

---

### Post by ZarathustraDK on 2009-04-25
Here's a novel idea. Using png's with an alpha-channel element to create silhouettes using the compiz skydome as a backdrop.

It solves a practical problem: It's hard to find 4 cool wallpapers which complement each other exactly the way you want it. With this, you can simply cut out the motif you're after, then use the skydome-art as a unifying element giving all four desktops a coherent expression.

It looks absolutely awesome when spinning the cube and using an animated skydome.

### Post by BwackNinja on 2009-04-25
> **jimbo99 said:**
> Can you explain the desktop applet that displays the song and lyrics?

I took eightmillion's conky lyrics python script, and hacked at it until it became sentient and self sufficient (read: detects song changes and updates itself and no longer uses conky) then I added the transparent background with rounded corners. Yay pango and cairo!

Then I also added a time display, a cpu usage graph, a ram usage graph, and a standard bar that isn't used anywhere, as well as using the conkyForecast.py script that is included in the "Conky - Mira" configuration the same way that conky does to get the weather.

It works great for displaying what I need it to, but I'll probably want to clean up the code a bit and add in support for a configuration file. I can attach the script if you want. The lyrics display depends on mpd and python-mpd, and the rest basically just requires pygtk.

---

### Post by sertse on 2009-04-25
Just minor changes. 

Here's also a nice trick.

If you're using the [Fission]("https://addons.mozilla.org/en-US/firefox/addon/1951") firefox addon, and want fission to use your gtk progress bar settings, create a file called userChrome.css and put this in your /home/(user)/.mozilla/firefox/(random numbers and letters)/chrome/ directory.

```
@namespace url("http://www.mozilla.org/keymaster/gatekeeper/there.is.only.xul"); /* set default namespace to XUL */


#urlbar[fission="fusion"] > #statusbar-icon .progress-bar
{
	-moz-appearance: progresschunk !important;
}
```

I took it from userChrome.css from the Elegant Brit theme. 

Hey etnllcarus, I noticed that the icons in your right click xfce menu are bigger than usual, how do you do that? Hope it's not just me seeing things.

---

### Post by Sin@Sin-Sacrifice on 2009-04-26
I know its already been done but I would like to see what people are doing with their desktop now. I'm pretty happy with the way mine turned out but now that my troubleshooting time is minimal and work is slow I would like to do some more customizations. Whether that be changing current ones or adding more to my already semi-cluttered desktop. The clutter is, although, functional for everyday use so I don't mind so much. 

For all you IT guys out there that love simple and only minutely customized desktops for work purposes... this isn't the thread for you. Please leave your comments about bloated linux this and "I don't see the point" that to yourself. This is for people who like that sort of thing.

So post your pictures please... 

Picture description:  Pic 1- This is my setup using Ubuntu Studio Hardy and Gnome with compiz-fusion and emerald. My favorite part of this is my terminal. Painted to the background and made to say "Killmandline" as oppose to the usual boring user@user-interface prompt. A stolen, but slightly modified, conky which I'm going to change the colors of once done posting. Temp sensors, weather, video background monitor, volume control, time and date, trash can, window switcher, and gnomenu on the tool bar. And finally my awn. I have windows opening like geanie bottle smoke and closing in a ball of blue flames along with a few other compiz effects.

Pic 2- Cube in space. I love it. Got the backgrounds from some theme at gnome-look and the cube background is actually a pretty high res hubble picture.

### Post by rub3nmv on 2009-04-27
> **oack said:**
> I like


I ask you what kdemod (arch) is like to install also why the change to kubuntu? 

cheers

Well, despite Archlinux is not a 'for-linux-begginers' distro, is not hard to install and setup if you follow carefully some guides (and you can learn a lot about Linux). If you're thinking on try Archlinux I would recomend you [[COLOR="Blue"]Chakra[/COLOR]]("http://kdemod.ath.cx/"), wich is a Archlinux-kdemod distro with a graphical installer.

And the main reason I'm thinking on moving to Kubuntu is the large repository and precompiled packages, on Arch there's [[COLOR="Blue"]AUR[/COLOR]]("http://wiki.archlinux.org/index.php/AUR_User_Guidelines") (in the case you can't find what you're searching for on the kdemod and archlinux repos), but it takes time to compile and sometimes I have troubles with dependencies (i.e. synapse im client and qyoto), etc.

---

### Post by Giant Speck on 2009-04-29
> **Sand & Mercury said:**
> Haha, I was using that wallpaper you got there for a brief spell. How's the RC cracking? Anything noticeably different since the beta?

I'm getting the same weird RAM vibe that I did from the beta.  RAM usage is moderate, with only Chrome running it is using 517MB out of 1000MB.  However, everything is moving quite smoothly.  Even if I'm using several programs at once, it still feels just as smooth.  I'm guessing that Windows 7 uses RAM in a much more efficient manner than its predecessors.

The beta has also done a lot of polishing of the UI.  It has removed a whole bunch of color inconsistencies and has moved away from the Vista color scheme altogether, replacing the turquoise for a nice, calm light blue. 

I haven't really dug into it yet, but so far, the experience has been positive. :)

---

### Post by etnlIcarus on 2009-04-30
> **Giant Speck said:**
> Now, *that* is awesome.  The golden brown really looks great with **your theme**.

Speaking of which, I know I've said this before but I think it's finally almost bug-free. I don't know what I did but qgtkstyle is now colouring text correctly on all widgets. The only bug I can think of is some Gtk+ apps aren't honouring my xthickness settings for tooltips.

```
widget "*GtkTooltip*" style "theme-tooltip"
widget_class "*<GtkTooltip>" style "theme-tooltip"
class "*GtkTooltip*" style "theme-tooltip"

widget "*gtk-tooltip*" style "theme-tooltip"
widget_class "*<gtk-tooltip>" style "theme-tooltip"
class "*gtk-tooltip*" style "theme-tooltip"
```

[url=http://img524.imageshack.us/img524/5712/wrongright.jpg][img]http://img83.imageshack.us/img83/8762/wrongrightsml.jpg[/img]
http://img524.imageshack.us/img524/5712/wrongright.jpg[/url]

Anything particularly out of place with my matches? I know one set of matches does nothing but I can't remember which set.

### Post by Giant Speck on 2009-04-30
> **eightmillion said:**
> I haven't posted a desktop in a while. Here's my current.

[[IMG]http://g.imagehost.org/0857/desktop928192.jpg[/IMG]]("http://g.imagehost.org/view/0402/desktop928192")

There are only two things I don't like about your screenshot:

1.)  I really like the drop down menus.  First of all, I think it looks weird because the menus are set into the window instead of sticking out.  You know what I'm saying?  Also, I don't like the arrows that Bespin uses.  They just don't look right.  A simple arrow would be better.

2.)  The panel is too transparent.  It would look better with alpha blur.  I don't know if you can use alpha blur with KDE and Plasma, though.

Other than that, I think it looks great!  I really like the sliders!

---

### Post by eightmillion on 2009-04-30
> **Giant Speck said:**
> There are only two things I don't like about your screenshot:

1.)  I really like the drop down menus.  First of all, I think it looks weird because the menus are set into the window instead of sticking out.  You know what I'm saying?  Also, I don't like the arrows that Bespin uses.  They just don't look right.  A simple arrow would be better.

2.)  The panel is too transparent.  It would look better with alpha blur.  I don't know if you can use alpha blur with KDE and Plasma, though.

Other than that, I think it looks great!  I really like the sliders!
Thanks. I don't know if you meant to say that you don't like the drop menus? I like them, and changing them is just a matter of toggling a checkbox in the bespin config. I kind of like the arrows too, although it would be nice to be able to change them.

About the alpha blur, you can use alpha blur with KDE 4, but not with my graphics card (Intel X3100). It's funny, I can boot up a Windows XP VM and use alpha blur with Window Blinds (it's software, but still). When I first got my laptop and it had Vista on it, alpha blur worked, but on Linux it's a no go with KDE or Compiz. It's annoying knowing that it's possible with my card, but know one seems to care enough to make it work. :(
